{\footnotesize\ttfamily \+\_\+allow\+\_\+reckless\+\_\+class\+\_\+checks (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{depth = {\ttfamily 3} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Allow instance and class checks for special stdlib modules.
The abc and functools modules indiscriminately call isinstance() and
issubclass() on the whole MRO of a user class, which may contain protocols.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a7c331e8a210aa7da0cee603877d2e2e2}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a7c331e8a210aa7da0cee603877d2e2e2} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!assert\_never@{assert\_never}}
\index{assert\_never@{assert\_never}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{assert\_never()}{assert\_never()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily  \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a69f26a00f1f960ceb4cc9c3c6ce95ebd}{Never}} assert\+\_\+never (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a69f26a00f1f960ceb4cc9c3c6ce95ebd}{Never}}}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+arg }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Assert to the type checker that a line of code is unreachable.

Example::

    def int_or_str(arg: int | str) -> None:
        match arg:
            case int():
                print("It's an int")
            case str():
                print("It's a str")
            case _:
                assert_never(arg)

If a type checker finds that a call to assert_never() is
reachable, it will emit an error.

At runtime, this throws an exception when called.\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_ae227fc2105404c5399ebbdfd4b3d322d}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_ae227fc2105404c5399ebbdfd4b3d322d} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!assert\_type@{assert\_type}}
\index{assert\_type@{assert\_type}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{assert\_type()}{assert\_type()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily assert\+\_\+type (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+val,  }\item[{}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+typ }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Assert (to the type checker) that the value is of the given type.

When the type checker encounters a call to assert_type(), it
emits an error if the value is not of the specified type::

    def greet(name: str) -> None:
        assert_type(name, str)  # ok
        assert_type(name, int)  # type checker error

At runtime this returns the first argument unchanged and otherwise
does nothing.
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source_l01189}{1189}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source}{typing\+\_\+extensions.\+py}}.

higher order function which adds, removes or transforms parameters of a
callable.

For example::

   Callable[Concatenate[int, P], int]

See PEP 612 for detailed information.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_afaa652140e530a898c3a2a9b54804e8d}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_afaa652140e530a898c3a2a9b54804e8d} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!dataclass\_transform@{dataclass\_transform}}
\index{dataclass\_transform@{dataclass\_transform}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{dataclass\_transform()}{dataclass\_transform()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily  typing.\+Callable\mbox{[}\mbox{[}\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_adf1f3edb9115acb0a1e04209b7a9937b}{T}}\mbox{]}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_adf1f3edb9115acb0a1e04209b7a9937b}{T}}\mbox{]} dataclass\+\_\+transform (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}bool }]{eq\+\_\+default = {\ttfamily True},  }\item[{bool }]{order\+\_\+default = {\ttfamily False},  }\item[{bool }]{kw\+\_\+only\+\_\+default = {\ttfamily False},  }\item[{bool }]{frozen\+\_\+default = {\ttfamily False},  }\item[{typing.\+Tuple\mbox{[}             typing.\+Union\mbox{[}typing.\+Type\mbox{[}typing.\+Any\mbox{]}, typing.\+Callable\mbox{[}..., typing.\+Any\mbox{]}\mbox{]},             ...         \mbox{]} }]{field\+\_\+specifiers = {\ttfamily ()},  }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}typing.\+Any}]{kwargs }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Decorator that marks a function, class, or metaclass as providing
dataclass-like behavior.

Example:

    from pip._vendor.typing_extensions import dataclass_transform

    _T = TypeVar("_T")

    # Used on a decorator function
    @dataclass_transform()
    def create_model(cls: type[_T]) -> type[_T]:
        ...
        return cls

    @create_model
    class CustomerModel:
        id: int
        name: str

    # Used on a base class
    @dataclass_transform()
    class ModelBase: ...

    class CustomerModel(ModelBase):
        id: int
        name: str

    # Used on a metaclass
    @dataclass_transform()
    class ModelMeta(type): ...

    class ModelBase(metaclass=ModelMeta): ...

    class CustomerModel(ModelBase):
        id: int
        name: str

Each of the ``CustomerModel`` classes defined in this example will now
behave similarly to a dataclass created with the ``@dataclasses.dataclass``
decorator. For example, the type checker will synthesize an ``__init__``
method.

The arguments to this decorator can be used to customize this behavior:
- ``eq_default`` indicates whether the ``eq`` parameter is assumed to be
  True or False if it is omitted by the caller.
- ``order_default`` indicates whether the ``order`` parameter is
  assumed to be True or False if it is omitted by the caller.
- ``kw_only_default`` indicates whether the ``kw_only`` parameter is
  assumed to be True or False if it is omitted by the caller.
- ``frozen_default`` indicates whether the ``frozen`` parameter is
  assumed to be True or False if it is omitted by the caller.
- ``field_specifiers`` specifies a static list of supported classes
  or functions that describe fields, similar to ``dataclasses.field()``.

At runtime, this decorator records its arguments in the
``__dataclass_transform__`` attribute on the decorated object.

See PEP 681 for details.\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source_l02360}{2360}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source}{typing\+\_\+extensions.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a86dc3a0bc7f51cd0a0ad1e0d5b26ed85}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a86dc3a0bc7f51cd0a0ad1e0d5b26ed85} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!deprecated@{deprecated}}
\index{deprecated@{deprecated}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{deprecated()}{deprecated()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily  typing.\+Callable\mbox{[}\mbox{[}\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a15d920713a31c7f6fa105e0ab1e5085a}{\+\_\+T}}\mbox{]}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a15d920713a31c7f6fa105e0ab1e5085a}{\+\_\+T}}\mbox{]} deprecated (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{str}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+msg,  }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}typing.\+Optional\mbox{[}typing.\+Type\mbox{[}Warning\mbox{]}\mbox{]} }]{category = {\ttfamily DeprecationWarning},  }\item[{int }]{stacklevel = {\ttfamily 1} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Indicate that a class, function or overload is deprecated.

Usage:

    @deprecated("Use B instead")
    class A:
        pass

    @deprecated("Use g instead")
    def f():
        pass

    @overload
    @deprecated("int support is deprecated")
    def g(x: int) -> int: ...
    @overload
    def g(x: str) -> int: ...

When this decorator is applied to an object, the type checker
will generate a diagnostic on usage of the deprecated object.

The warning specified by ``category`` will be emitted on use
of deprecated objects. For functions, that happens on calls;
for classes, on instantiation. If the ``category`` is ``None``,
no warning is emitted. The ``stacklevel`` determines where the
warning is emitted. If it is ``1`` (the default), the warning
is emitted at the direct caller of the deprecated object; if it
is higher, it is emitted further up the stack.

The decorator sets the ``__deprecated__``
attribute on the decorated object to the deprecation message
passed to the decorator. If applied to an overload, the decorator
must be after the ``@overload`` decorator for the attribute to
exist on the overload as returned by ``get_overloads()``.

See PEP 702 for details.\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source_l02492}{2492}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source}{typing\+\_\+extensions.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a639e1c0008b09189dab47b8e8167b9cc}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a639e1c0008b09189dab47b8e8167b9cc} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!final@{final}}
\index{final@{final}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{final()}{final()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily final (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{f }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}This decorator can be used to indicate to type checkers that
the decorated method cannot be overridden, and decorated class
cannot be subclassed. For example:

    class Base:
        @final
        def done(self) -> None:
            ...
    class Sub(Base):
        def done(self) -> None:  # Error reported by type checker
            ...
    @final
    class Leaf:
        ...
    class Other(Leaf):  # Error reported by type checker
        ...

There is no runtime checking of these properties. The decorator
sets the ``__final__`` attribute to ``True`` on the decorated object
to allow runtime introspection.
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source_l00284}{284}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source}{typing\+\_\+extensions.\+py}}.

\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!get\_args@{get\_args}}
\index{get\_args@{get\_args}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_args()}{get\_args()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily get\+\_\+args (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{tp }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Get type arguments with all substitutions performed.

For unions, basic simplifications used by Union constructor are performed.
Examples::
    get_args(Dict[str, int]) == (str, int)
    get_args(int) == ()
    get_args(Union[int, Union[T, int], str][int]) == (int, str)
    get_args(Union[int, Tuple[T, int]][str]) == (int, Tuple[str, int])
    get_args(Callable[[], T][int]) == ([], int)
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a558db46b99797faa899fb14ca26bb00a}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a558db46b99797faa899fb14ca26bb00a}

\index{get\_origin@{get\_origin}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_origin()}{get\_origin()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily get\+\_\+origin (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{tp }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Get the unsubscripted version of a type.

This supports generic types, Callable, Tuple, Union, Literal, Final, ClassVar
and Annotated. Return None for unsupported types. Examples::

    get_origin(Literal[42]) is Literal
    get_origin(int) is None
    get_origin(ClassVar[int]) is ClassVar
    get_origin(Generic) is Generic
    get_origin(Generic[T]) is Generic
    get_origin(Union[T, int]) is Union
    get_origin(List[Tuple[T, T]][int]) == list
    get_origin(P.args) is P
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_afbd174a75b7e93c596f10158ed489413}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_afbd174a75b7e93c596f10158ed489413} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!get\_original\_bases@{get\_original\_bases}}
\index{get\_original\_bases@{get\_original\_bases}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_original\_bases()}{get\_original\_bases()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily get\+\_\+original\+\_\+bases (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+cls }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return the class's "original" bases prior to modification by `__mro_entries__`.

Examples::

    from typing import TypeVar, Generic
    from pip._vendor.typing_extensions import NamedTuple, TypedDict

    T = TypeVar("T")
    class Foo(Generic[T]): ...
    class Bar(Foo[int], float): ...
    class Baz(list[str]): ...
    Eggs = NamedTuple("Eggs", [("a", int), ("b", str)])
    Spam = TypedDict("Spam", {"a": int, "b": str})

    assert get_original_bases(Bar) == (Foo[int], float)
    assert get_original_bases(Baz) == (list[str],)
    assert get_original_bases(Eggs) == (NamedTuple,)
    assert get_original_bases(Spam) == (TypedDict,)
    assert get_original_bases(int) == (object,)
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_ac62f7fd4777bbd20265442c44aedad2d}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_ac62f7fd4777bbd20265442c44aedad2d} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!get\_protocol\_members@{get\_protocol\_members}}
\index{get\_protocol\_members@{get\_protocol\_members}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_protocol\_members()}{get\_protocol\_members()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily  typing.\+Frozen\+Set\mbox{[}str\mbox{]} get\+\_\+protocol\+\_\+members (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{type}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+tp }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return the set of members defined in a Protocol.

Example::

    >>> from typing_extensions import Protocol, get_protocol_members
    >>> class P(Protocol):
    ...     def a(self) -> str: ...
    ...     b: int
    >>> get_protocol_members(P)
    frozenset({'a', 'b'})

Raise a TypeError for arguments that are not Protocols.
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source_l03011}{3011}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source}{typing\+\_\+extensions.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a5781dc3dd0e9ce31a25b333386200a90}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a5781dc3dd0e9ce31a25b333386200a90} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!get\_type\_hints@{get\_type\_hints}}
\index{get\_type\_hints@{get\_type\_hints}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_type\_hints()}{get\_type\_hints()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily get\+\_\+type\+\_\+hints (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{obj,  }\item[{}]{globalns = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{prime__search_8m_a6f6ccfcf58b31cb6412107d9d5281426}{None}}},  }\item[{}]{localns = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{prime__search_8m_a6f6ccfcf58b31cb6412107d9d5281426}{None}}},  }\item[{}]{include\+\_\+extras = {\ttfamily False} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return type hints for an object.

This is often the same as obj.__annotations__, but it handles
forward references encoded as string literals, adds Optional[t] if a
default value equal to None is set and recursively replaces all
'Annotated[T, ...]', 'Required[T]' or 'NotRequired[T]' with 'T'
(unless 'include_extras=True').

The argument may be a module, class, method, or function. The annotations
are returned as a dictionary. For classes, annotations include also
inherited members.

TypeError is raised if the argument is not of a type that can contain
annotations, and an empty dictionary is returned if no annotations are
present.

BEWARE -- the behavior of globalns and localns is counterintuitive
(unless you are familiar with how eval() and exec() work).  The
search order is locals first, then globals.

- If no dict arguments are passed, an attempt is made to use the
  globals from obj (or the respective module's globals for classes),
  and these are also used as the locals.  If the object does not appear
  to have globals, an empty dictionary is used.

- If one dict argument is passed, it is used for both globals and
  locals.

- If two dict arguments are passed, they specify globals and
  locals, respectively.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{is\_protocol()}{is\_protocol()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily  bool is\+\_\+protocol (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{type}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+tp }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return True if the given type is a Protocol.

Example::

    >>> from typing_extensions import Protocol, is_protocol
    >>> class P(Protocol):
    ...     def a(self) -> str: ...
    ...     b: int
    >>> is_protocol(P)
    True
    >>> is_protocol(int)
    False
\end{DoxyVerb}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Check if an annotation is a TypedDict class

For example::
    class Film(TypedDict):
        title: str
        year: int

    is_typeddict(Film)  # => True
    is_typeddict(Union[list, str])  # => False
\end{DoxyVerb}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily Literal\+String (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self,  }\item[{}]{params }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Represents an arbitrary literal string.

Example::

  from pip._vendor.typing_extensions import LiteralString

  def query(sql: LiteralString) -> ...:
      ...

  query("SELECT * FROM table")  # ok
  query(f"SELECT * FROM {input()}")  # not ok

See PEP 675 for details.\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a1f6eab2e0a19addfcd935793645be85f}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a1f6eab2e0a19addfcd935793645be85f} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!NamedTuple@{NamedTuple}}
\index{NamedTuple@{NamedTuple}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{NamedTuple()}{NamedTuple()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily Named\+Tuple (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+typename,  }\item[{}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+fields = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a63ea03a90f1b90572338d8f16fd2438e}{\+\_\+marker}}},  }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{kwargs }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Typed version of namedtuple.

Usage::

    class Employee(NamedTuple):
        name: str
        id: int

This is equivalent to::

    Employee = collections.namedtuple('Employee', ['name', 'id'])

The resulting class has an extra __annotations__ attribute, giving a
dict that maps field names to types.  (The field names are also in
the _fields attribute, which is part of the namedtuple API.)
An alternative equivalent functional syntax is also accepted::

    Employee = NamedTuple('Employee', [('name', str), ('id', int)])
\end{DoxyVerb}

\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!Never@{Never}}
\index{Never@{Never}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Never()}{Never()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily Never (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self,  }\item[{}]{params }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}The bottom type, a type that has no members.

This can be used to define a function that should never be
called, or a function that never returns::

    from pip._vendor.typing_extensions import Never

    def never_call_me(arg: Never) -> None:
        pass

    def int_or_str(arg: int | str) -> None:
        never_call_me(arg)  # type checker error
        match arg:
            case int():
                print("It's an int")
            case str():
                print("It's a str")
            case _:
                never_call_me(arg)  # ok, arg is of type Never\end{DoxyVerb}

\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!NotRequired@{NotRequired}}
\index{NotRequired@{NotRequired}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{NotRequired()}{NotRequired()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily Not\+Required (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self,  }\item[{}]{parameters }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}A special typing construct to mark a key of a TypedDict as
potentially missing. For example:

    class Movie(TypedDict):
        title: str
        year: NotRequired[int]

    m = Movie(
        title='The Matrix',  # typechecker error if key is omitted
        year=1999,
    )
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_ab5b08d386259bc828eed34cdb248c39f}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_ab5b08d386259bc828eed34cdb248c39f} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!overload@{overload}}
\index{overload@{overload}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{overload()}{overload()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily overload (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{func }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Decorator for overloaded functions/methods.

In a stub file, place two or more stub definitions for the same
function in a row, each decorated with @overload.  For example:

@overload
def utf8(value: None) -> None: ...
@overload
def utf8(value: bytes) -> bytes: ...
@overload
def utf8(value: str) -> bytes: ...

In a non-stub file (i.e. a regular .py file), do the same but
follow it with an implementation.  The implementation should *not*
be decorated with @overload.  For example:

@overload
def utf8(value: None) -> None: ...
@overload
def utf8(value: bytes) -> bytes: ...
@overload
def utf8(value: str) -> bytes: ...
def utf8(value):
    # implementation goes here

The overloads for a function can be retrieved at runtime using the
get_overloads() function.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{override()}{override()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily  \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a7ca0731de93b000fa4b206ad3793f8c7}{\+\_\+F}} override (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a7ca0731de93b000fa4b206ad3793f8c7}{\+\_\+F}}}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+arg }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Indicate that a method is intended to override a method in a base class.

Usage:

    class Base:
        def method(self) -> None: ...
            pass

    class Child(Base):
        @override
        def method(self) -> None:
            super().method()

When this decorator is applied to a method, the type checker will
validate that it overrides a method with the same name on a base class.
This helps prevent bugs that may occur when a base class is changed
without an equivalent change to a child class.

There is no runtime checking of these properties. The decorator
sets the ``__override__`` attribute to ``True`` on the decorated object
to allow runtime introspection.

See PEP 698 for details.\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source_l02451}{2451}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{typing__extensions_8py_source}{typing\+\_\+extensions.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_ac84c07306ac3791a4078e9107e93450c}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_ac84c07306ac3791a4078e9107e93450c} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!Required@{Required}}
\index{Required@{Required}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{Required()}{Required()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily Required (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self,  }\item[{}]{parameters }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}A special typing construct to mark a key of a total=False TypedDict
as required. For example:

    class Movie(TypedDict, total=False):
        title: Required[str]
        year: int

    m = Movie(
        title='The Matrix',  # typechecker error if key is omitted
        year=1999,
    )

There is no runtime checking that a required key is actually provided
when instantiating a related TypedDict.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_abdda3db25ac9cb375f44987e2965dceb}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_abdda3db25ac9cb375f44987e2965dceb} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!reveal\_type@{reveal\_type}}
\index{reveal\_type@{reveal\_type}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{reveal\_type()}{reveal\_type()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily  \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_adf1f3edb9115acb0a1e04209b7a9937b}{T}} reveal\+\_\+type (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_adf1f3edb9115acb0a1e04209b7a9937b}{T}}}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+obj }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Reveal the inferred type of a variable.

When a static type checker encounters a call to ``reveal_type()``,
it will emit the inferred type of the argument::

    x: int = 1
    reveal_type(x)

Running a static type checker (e.g., ``mypy``) on this example
will produce output similar to 'Revealed type is "builtins.int"'.

At runtime, the function prints the runtime type of the
argument and returns it unchanged.\end{DoxyVerb}

\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!runtime\_checkable@{runtime\_checkable}}
\index{runtime\_checkable@{runtime\_checkable}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{runtime\_checkable()}{runtime\_checkable()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily runtime\+\_\+checkable (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{cls }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Mark a protocol class as a runtime protocol, so that it
can be used with isinstance() and issubclass(). Raise TypeError
if applied to a non-protocol class.

This allows a simple-minded structural check very similar to the
one-offs in collections.abc such as Hashable.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a1488f98e93da60d10f3e8d809f9965d9}\label{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a1488f98e93da60d10f3e8d809f9965d9} 
\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!TypedDict@{TypedDict}}
\index{TypedDict@{TypedDict}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{TypedDict()}{TypedDict()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily Typed\+Dict (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+typename,  }\item[{}]{\+\_\+\+\_\+fields = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespacepip_1_1__vendor_1_1typing__extensions_a63ea03a90f1b90572338d8f16fd2438e}{\+\_\+marker}}},  }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{total = {\ttfamily True},  }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{kwargs }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}A simple typed namespace. At runtime it is equivalent to a plain dict.

TypedDict creates a dictionary type such that a type checker will expect all
instances to have a certain set of keys, where each key is
associated with a value of a consistent type. This expectation
is not checked at runtime.

Usage::

    class Point2D(TypedDict):
        x: int
        y: int
        label: str

    a: Point2D = {'x': 1, 'y': 2, 'label': 'good'}  # OK
    b: Point2D = {'z': 3, 'label': 'bad'}           # Fails type check

    assert Point2D(x=1, y=2, label='first') == dict(x=1, y=2, label='first')

The type info can be accessed via the Point2D.__annotations__ dict, and
the Point2D.__required_keys__ and Point2D.__optional_keys__ frozensets.
TypedDict supports an additional equivalent form::

    Point2D = TypedDict('Point2D', {'x': int, 'y': int, 'label': str})

By default, all keys must be present in a TypedDict. It is possible
to override this by specifying totality::

    class Point2D(TypedDict, total=False):
        x: int
        y: int

This means that a Point2D TypedDict can have any of the keys omitted. A type
checker is only expected to support a literal False or True as the value of
the total argument. True is the default, and makes all items defined in the
class body be required.

The Required and NotRequired special forms can also be used to mark
individual keys as being required or not required::

    class Point2D(TypedDict):
        x: int  # the "x" key must always be present (Required is the default)
        y: NotRequired[int]  # the "y" key can be omitted

See PEP 655 for more details on Required and NotRequired.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\index{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}!TypeGuard@{TypeGuard}}
\index{TypeGuard@{TypeGuard}!pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions@{pip.\_vendor.typing\_extensions}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{TypeGuard()}{TypeGuard()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily Type\+Guard (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self,  }\item[{}]{parameters }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Special typing form used to annotate the return type of a user-defined
type guard function.  ``TypeGuard`` only accepts a single type argument.
At runtime, functions marked this way should return a boolean.

``TypeGuard`` aims to benefit *type narrowing* -- a technique used by static
type checkers to determine a more precise type of an expression within a
program's code flow.  Usually type narrowing is done by analyzing
conditional code flow and applying the narrowing to a block of code.  The
conditional expression here is sometimes referred to as a "type guard".

Sometimes it would be convenient to use a user-defined boolean function
as a type guard.  Such a function should use ``TypeGuard[...]`` as its
return type to alert static type checkers to this intention.

Using  ``-> TypeGuard`` tells the static type checker that for a given
function:

1. The return value is a boolean.
2. If the return value is ``True``, the type of its argument
is the type inside ``TypeGuard``.

For example::

    def is_str(val: Union[str, float]):
        # "isinstance" type guard
        if isinstance(val, str):
            # Type of ``val`` is narrowed to ``str``
            ...
        else:
            # Else, type of ``val`` is narrowed to ``float``.
            ...

Strict type narrowing is not enforced -- ``TypeB`` need not be a narrower
form of ``TypeA`` (it can even be a wider form) and this may lead to
type-unsafe results.  The main reason is to allow for things like
narrowing ``List[object]`` to ``List[str]`` even though the latter is not
a subtype of the former, since ``List`` is invariant.  The responsibility of
writing type-safe type guards is left to the user.

``TypeGuard`` also works with type variables.  For more information, see
PEP 647 (User-Defined Type Guards).
\end{DoxyVerb}
